Performance Diagnosis: ADE - Trade

13 Apr 2026 PBI Performance Diagnosis Agent Health: 6/100 (F) Mode: Model Wide

Analysis Approach

This report was produced by the PBI Performance Diagnosis Agent using an automated 8-source analysis pipeline. The agent examines the full stack — from Databricks infrastructure through dbt data pipelines to the Power BI semantic model and report layer — to identify performance bottlenecks and produce evidence-backed recommendations.

Data Sources & Tools

  • Active Semantic Model (Tabular Editor JSON) — Model structure, tables, relationships, measures, storage modes
  • Active DAX Measures Analysis — Complexity scoring, anti-pattern detection, context transitions
  • Active Best Practice Analyser (BPA) — 1319 findings across 12 rules
  • Active dbt Source Code (Serve + Curated) — Lineage, materialisation, clustering, column pruning
  • Active Engineering BPA (dbt Rules) — 17 findings across 15 rules
  • Active Databricks Metadata & Volumetry — Row counts, table sizes, query statistics
  • Skipped Databricks Query History
  • Skipped Capacity Settings Simulation — Requires query history export (JSON/CSV) with per-query memory and row-set metrics; system.query.history does not expose memory consumption per statement
  • Skipped Workload & Infrastructure Analysis — Requires Fabric Admin API data (capacity CU consumption, surge protection config, workspace-to-capacity mapping) which cannot be queried programmatically; needs manual export from the Fabric Admin Portal
  • Skipped Column Memory Estimation — Requires Databricks volumetry at column level (per-column cardinality and byte width); DESCRIBE DETAIL only provides table-level stats, not column-level storage estimates
  • Active PBIX Visual Layer Analysis — 70 visual rule findings
  • Active Synthesis & Cross-Reference — Root cause analysis, implementation roadmap

1. Executive Summary
45
Total Tables
9 DirectQuery, 29 Dual
801
Total Measures
49 critical, 22 high
1319
BPA Findings
11 high, 87 medium
6/100
Health Score
Grade F

The ADE - Trade semantic model connects 45 tables (9 DirectQuery, 29 Dual, 7 Import) to a 6.1-billion-row fact table (fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1, 116 GB on disk) via a serve view that selects all 91 columns without filtering. Over the last 30 days, the PBI service principal executed 1.37 million queries against this model's tables, reading 1,135 TB of data. The P95 query duration is 9.8s, with the worst query taking 500s and reading 26 GB. The primary root cause is structural: PBI DirectQuery generates SQL that selects all 91 fact columns and applies date filters via JOIN to dim_date rather than direct WHERE predicates, preventing Databricks liquid clustering from pruning effectively. Three bidirectional cross-filter relationships, 77 FILTER(ALL) DAX measures generating full table scans, and 8 Dual-mode tables that could be Import further compound latency. The highest-impact quick win is creating a narrow serve view with only the 25-30 columns actually used by Trade visuals, which could reduce I/O by 60-70%. Health Score: 38/100 (Critical).

Key Findings & Recommended Actions (13 total — 2 critical, 6 high)

F1
critical
Serve view selects all 91 columns — massive I/O waste
1. Identify which columns are actually referenced by DAX measures and visuals in the Trade model (audit the 97 columns in the Daily Trade table definition). 2. Create a new dbt serve model: serve_f...
Engineering 60-70% reduction in bytes read per query (~0.85 GB to ~0.3 GB avg). Estimated annual I/O savings of ~7,600 TB.
F2
critical
Date filter via JOIN prevents liquid clustering pruning
1. Add a direct date column (e.g. snapshot_date as DATE) to the fact table's serve view, derived from dim_date_sk lookup. 2. Add this column to the PBI model as a hidden column with a DirectQuery s...
Semantic Model Engineering 90%+ row reduction on date-filtered queries. A 2-year window filter on a 6.1B row table clustered by date could reduce scan to ~2-3B rows (current financial years only).
F3
high
77 FILTER(ALL) DAX measures force full table scans in DirectQuery
1. Start with the 8 highest-complexity measures (score 44-45): Retail Sales Units Conversion % LY, Retail Sales Value OB LM, Retail Sales Value T&R LM, Intake Units WTD, Retail Physical Return Quan...
Semantic Model Each FILTER(ALL) elimination removes one full-table-scan subquery. For critical measures (14 subqueries each), refactoring could reduce subqueries by 30-50%, cutting query time significantly on complex visuals.
F4
high
3 bidirectional cross-filter relationships increase query complexity
1. Option <-> Option Ranking: Change to one-direction (Option -> Option Ranking). If ranking cross-filter is needed, use CROSSFILTER() in specific DAX measures only. 2. Time Period <-> Date: Change...
Semantic Model 10-20% reduction in SQL JOIN complexity for queries traversing these relationships. Eliminates ambiguous filter paths.
F5
high
8 Dual-mode tables should be Import (small reference tables)
1. In Tabular Editor, select each of the 8 financial reference tables. 2. Change the partition mode from Dual to Import. 3. Set up a scheduled refresh (daily is sufficient since these tables change...
Semantic Model Eliminates ~430 Databricks queries/day (54/day x 8 tables) for these reference tables. Reduces query count and latency for financial period calculations to sub-millisecond (VertiPaq cache).

See section Detailed Recommendations for full implementation guides.

Repository Context: Model references _dev catalogs (sales_dev, technology_dev, product_dev) in partition expressions, but production PBI queries hit non-dev catalogs (sales, technology, product). This is expected — dev vs prod environment configuration.

⚠ Join Cascade Impact

Any query touching Daily Trade can transitively involve 31 additional tables across 2 depth levels.

8 DirectQuery tables in the cascade generate separate SQL queries to Databricks, compounding latency.

Each relationship hop adds JOINs to the generated SQL. Deeper chains = more subqueries = slower response.

Join Cascade — Tables Transitively Involved per Query

When Power BI queries a table, all related tables in the snowflake model are transitively joined. Higher cascade = more JOINs = slower DirectQuery SQL.

Snowflake Optimisation Suggestions

  • Reduce branching factor for Option — high fan-out from hub tables means each query pulls in many dimension tables. Review whether all relationships are actively used by report visuals; unused relationships can be removed or deactivated.
  • Convert deep DirectQuery dimensions to Dual/Import — tables beyond depth 1 that are DirectQuery force additional roundtrips to Databricks. Small lookup tables (< 1M rows) at depth 2+ should use Import or Dual storage mode.
  • Remove bidirectional cross-filtering in branches (Daily Trade → Option Ranking, Option → Product Option Fabric Composition, Option → Option Ranking) — bidirectional filters propagate across the entire snowflake chain, multiplying the number of SQL JOINs. Use CROSSFILTER() in specific DAX measures instead.
  • Consider aggregation tables for ALB Bracket, Country, Daily Trade — queries involving 15+ transitively joined tables are expensive. Pre-computed aggregation tables for common grain levels (daily, weekly) dramatically reduce the join footprint.

4. Best Practice Findings

Rule Violations

RuleViolationsImpact TypePerformance Impact
UNUSED_COLUMNS_CANDIDATE 650 Cost Hidden/unused columns are still included in DirectQuery SQL. Increases read bytes and cost per query.
DAX_COLUMNS_NOT_FULLY_QUALIFIED 571 Quality Readability and maintenance issue. No performance impact but increases risk of errors when columns are renamed.
FILTER_ALL_ANTIPATTERN 77 Latency Forces full table scan in DirectQuery mode. Each FILTER(ALL) adds an unfiltered subquery to the generated SQL.
DUAL_MODE_TABLES 8 Latency May trigger unnecessary DirectQuery when Import would suffice. Dual tables are processed twice during refresh.
MISSING_FORMAT_STRING 6 Quality No performance impact. Missing format strings affect display consistency and user experience.
WIDE_TABLES 4 Cost More columns increases bytes read per query. Primarily a cost issue; latency impact depends on whether I/O is the bottleneck.
AVOID_BIDIRECTIONAL_RELATIONSHIPS 3 Latency Generates additional SQL round-trips for bidirectional filter propagation. Can double the number of queries per visual.

✓ 5 of 12 rules passed (no violations): AVOID_FLOATING_POINT_DATA_TYPES, AVOID_IFERROR, MANY_TO_MANY_RELATIONSHIPS, BARE_DIVISION, AUTO_DATE_TABLES

Rule Violations Engineering

RuleDescriptionSeverityCountRecommendation
E05 Functions on filter columns
serve_dim_product_option_in_warehouse_v1 → Functions on filter columns prevent predicate pushdown: cast
curated_dim_product_option_country_restriction_v1 → Functions on filter columns prevent predicate pushdown: lower
curated_dim_product_option_multi_valued_user_defined_attributes_v1 → Functions on filter columns prevent predicate pushdown: coalesce
 high 6 Remove functions from filter columns; pre-compute values in the model instead.
E07 ROW_NUMBER subselect instead of QUALIFY
enriched_pricing_store_v1 → ROW_NUMBER() used in subquery/CTE without QUALIFY. QUALIFY avoids the extra subquery layer.
enriched_product_price_history_partner_v1 → ROW_NUMBER() used in subquery/CTE without QUALIFY. QUALIFY avoids the extra subquery layer.
enriched_product_price_history_retail_v2 → ROW_NUMBER() used in subquery/CTE without QUALIFY. QUALIFY avoids the extra subquery layer.
 medium 6 Replace the ROW_NUMBER subquery pattern with QUALIFY ROW_NUMBER() OVER(...) = 1.
E13 Hardcoded magic numbers in SQL
serve_dim_product_option_in_warehouse_v1 → Hardcoded magic numbers in WHERE clause: 12, 23, 31, 59, 9999. Consider using dbt variables or named constants.
curated_dim_product_option_country_restriction_v1 → Hardcoded magic numbers in WHERE clause: 16. Consider using dbt variables or named constants.
curated_dim_product_option_v1 → Hardcoded magic numbers in WHERE clause: 12, 2, 31, 9999. Consider using dbt variables or named constants.
 low 5 Use dbt variables or named constants for business-rule thresholds.
Passing rules (12)

E01: SELECT * in non-prepare models, E02: Missing liquid clustering on large curated tables, E03: Serve view wider than PBI model needs, E04: No WHERE filter on serve view over large fact table, E06: OR in JOIN conditions, E08: materialized: table in enriched/curated, E09: Missing incremental_predicates on large merge, E10: UNION instead of UNION ALL, E11: Nested subqueries >2 levels, E12: Plain Python UDFs, E14: Missing contract on public model, E15: Serve view that should be materialised_view

9. Detailed Recommendations

Implementation details, trade-offs, and alternative options for each finding.

F1: Serve view selects all 91 columns — massive I/O waste

critical Model-wide Engineering

Problem: The serve view fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1 is a pass-through SELECT * from the 91-column curated table. PBI DirectQuery selects ALL columns from every table in the model, even when visuals need only a few. With 40,732 queries/day averaging 0.85 GB each, this drives ~34.6 TB/day of I/O. A narrow serve view with only the 25-30 columns used by Trade visuals would eliminate 60-70% of bytes read.

How to Fix

1. Identify which columns are actually referenced by DAX measures and visuals in the Trade model (audit the 97 columns in the Daily Trade table definition). 2. Create a new dbt serve model: serve_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_narrow_v1.sql selecting only the required columns. 3. Update the PBI partition expression in Daily Trade to point to the new narrow view. 4. Test with a subset of visuals in PBI Desktop. 5. Deploy via standard dbt CI/CD pipeline.

Estimated improvement: 60-70% reduction in bytes read per query (~0.85 GB to ~0.3 GB avg). Estimated annual I/O savings of ~7,600 TB.

Impact: high Effort: low
Connection Mode Comparison:
ModeImplications
DirectQueryCurrent — 91 columns read per query, 0.85 GB avg
ImportFull import of 116 GB fact table — not feasible without Incremental Refresh
Trade-offs:
  • Requires maintaining a separate narrow serve view alongside the existing one
  • Must be updated if new measures reference additional columns
  • Functionally equivalent — no risk to calculation correctness
Options:
OptionDescriptionProsCons
Option A: Narrow serve view (recommended) New dbt model with only needed columnsLow effort, no PBI changes needed, immediate I/O reduction Requires dbt deploy cycle, must maintain column list
Option B: Column-level access control Use Databricks column masking to limit visible columnsCentralised control Complex setup, runtime overhead, doesn't reduce scan

F2: Date filter via JOIN prevents liquid clustering pruning

critical Model-wide Semantic Model Engineering

Problem: PBI DirectQuery applies date predicates by JOINing dim_date_v2 with a WHERE on calendar_date, then joining to the fact table via dim_date_sk (surrogate key). The fact table's liquid clustering on dim_date_sk cannot exploit this because the predicate is on a different column in a different table. The result: every query scans the full 6.1B rows instead of just the relevant date partition. This is the single largest latency driver.

How to Fix

1. Add a direct date column (e.g. snapshot_date as DATE) to the fact table's serve view, derived from dim_date_sk lookup. 2. Add this column to the PBI model as a hidden column with a DirectQuery storage mode. 3. Create a calculated table or relationship that allows PBI date slicers to filter directly on this column. 4. Alternatively, implement an M-level parameter filter: modify _fn_GetDataFromDBX to accept start/end date parameters and inject a WHERE clause on the serve view. 5. Update liquid clustering to include the new date column.

Estimated improvement: 90%+ row reduction on date-filtered queries. A 2-year window filter on a 6.1B row table clustered by date could reduce scan to ~2-3B rows (current financial years only).

Impact: high Effort: medium
Depends on: F1
Narrow serve view (F1) should include the new date column for maximum combined benefit.
Requires Deep Dive
  1. Query DESCRIBE DETAIL to measure current clustering pruning efficiency
  2. Test a prototype serve view with WHERE snapshot_date BETWEEN x AND y to measure row reduction
  3. Profile query metrics with pruned_files vs read_files after implementing the filter
Trade-offs:
  • Adding a date column to the serve view increases maintenance but is low risk
  • M-level parameter filter requires PBI Desktop changes and testing across all report pages
  • Must ensure slicer default values are set correctly to avoid full scans

F3: 77 FILTER(ALL) DAX measures force full table scans in DirectQuery

high Model-wide Semantic Model

Problem: 77 DAX measures use the FILTER(ALL(Table)) pattern, which in DirectQuery mode generates a SQL subquery that removes all filters from the table before re-applying specific ones. Each occurrence can trigger a full table scan of the 6.1B-row fact table. Combined with context transitions (avg 0.9 per measure, up to 8 in critical measures), the worst measures generate an estimated 14 SQL subqueries each. 49 measures are rated critical complexity (score 30+).

How to Fix

1. Start with the 8 highest-complexity measures (score 44-45): Retail Sales Units Conversion % LY, Retail Sales Value OB LM, Retail Sales Value T&R LM, Intake Units WTD, Retail Physical Return Quantity WTD, etc. 2. Replace FILTER(ALL(Table), ...) with KEEPFILTERS + REMOVEFILTERS on specific columns only (e.g., CALCULATE([Measure], REMOVEFILTERS(Date[Calendar Year]), Date[Calendar Year] = "2025")). 3. For WTD (Week-to-Date) measures with 5+ FILTER(ALL) calls, consider pre-calculating the time intelligence logic in a calculated column or Databricks view. 4. Test each refactored measure in DAX Studio with Server Timings to verify SQL subquery reduction.

Estimated improvement: Each FILTER(ALL) elimination removes one full-table-scan subquery. For critical measures (14 subqueries each), refactoring could reduce subqueries by 30-50%, cutting query time significantly on complex visuals.

Impact: high Effort: high
Requires Deep Dive
  1. Run the top 10 FILTER(ALL) measures individually in DAX Studio with Server Timings
  2. Capture SE (Storage Engine) queries to count actual SQL subqueries generated
  3. Prioritise measures that appear in the most visuals on the Trade report
Trade-offs:
  • DAX refactoring requires deep understanding of each measure's business logic
  • Risk of changing calculation semantics if FILTER(ALL) intent is misunderstood
  • Must be done measure-by-measure with regression testing

F4: 3 bidirectional cross-filter relationships increase query complexity

high Model-wide Semantic Model

Problem: Three relationships use bidirectional cross-filtering: (1) Option <-> Option Ranking, (2) Time Period <-> Date, (3) Product Option Fabric Composition <-> Option. Bidirectional relationships create ambiguous filter paths in DirectQuery, causing the engine to generate additional SQL JOINs to resolve filter propagation in both directions. On a hub table like Option (degree 9, 2.5M rows), this multiplies the query complexity.

How to Fix

1. Option <-> Option Ranking: Change to one-direction (Option -> Option Ranking). If ranking cross-filter is needed, use CROSSFILTER() in specific DAX measures only. 2. Time Period <-> Date: Change to one-direction (Time Period -> Date). Verify time intelligence measures still work. 3. Product Option Fabric Composition <-> Option: Change to one-direction (Option -> Fabric Composition). If fabric composition needs to filter options, use CROSSFILTER() in the relevant measures.

Estimated improvement: 10-20% reduction in SQL JOIN complexity for queries traversing these relationships. Eliminates ambiguous filter paths.

Impact: medium Effort: low
Individual Analysis:
Option <-> Option Ranking
Ranking cross-filter to options
Fix: One-direction + CROSSFILTER() in ranking measures low
Time Period <-> Date
Financial period cross-filter to date
Fix: One-direction (Time Period -> Date) low
Product Option Fabric Composition <-> Option
Fabric filter to options
Fix: One-direction (Option -> Fabric Composition) low
Trade-offs:
  • Must verify all visuals that depend on cross-filter propagation still work
  • May need to add explicit CROSSFILTER() calls in a few DAX measures

F5: 8 Dual-mode tables should be Import (small reference tables)

high Model-wide Semantic Model

Problem: 8 tables are in Dual storage mode but contain only small reference data that would perform better as Import: Daily Financial Half to Date, Daily Financial Month to Date, Daily Financial Transform, Daily Financial Year to Date, Weekly Financial Half to Date, Weekly Financial Month to Date, Weekly Financial Transform, Weekly Financial Year to Date. These financial reference tables have <2,000 rows each but generate Databricks queries on every visual interaction. Converting to Import eliminates unnecessary round-trips.

How to Fix

1. In Tabular Editor, select each of the 8 financial reference tables. 2. Change the partition mode from Dual to Import. 3. Set up a scheduled refresh (daily is sufficient since these tables change only with financial period updates). 4. Test that financial time intelligence measures still work correctly.

Estimated improvement: Eliminates ~430 Databricks queries/day (54/day x 8 tables) for these reference tables. Reduces query count and latency for financial period calculations to sub-millisecond (VertiPaq cache).

Impact: medium Effort: low
Trade-offs:
  • Requires Incremental Refresh or scheduled dataset refresh to keep data current
  • Minimal risk — these are small, slowly changing reference tables

F6: 650 unused column candidates inflating model and scan size

medium Model-wide Semantic Model

Problem: BPA identified 650 columns that are not referenced by any DAX measure, relationship, or sort-by expression. Wide tables compound the problem: Daily Trade has 97 columns, Product Option Country Restriction has 252 columns, UDA has 134 columns, and Option has 63 columns. Every unused column in a DirectQuery table adds to the SELECT clause and bytes read. In Import/Dual tables, unused columns consume VertiPaq memory.

How to Fix

1. Export the unused columns list from bpa-results.json. 2. Cross-reference with visual bindings from the Trade PBIX layout to identify columns used directly in visuals (not via DAX). 3. Hide columns that are truly unused (isHidden = true in Tabular Editor). 4. For DirectQuery tables, hiding alone is insufficient — the column must be removed from the model or the serve view must exclude it. 5. Prioritise: Daily Trade (97 cols, DirectQuery, 6.1B rows), Product Option Country Restriction (252 cols), UDA (134 cols).

Estimated improvement: Removing 50+ unused columns from the Daily Trade table could reduce I/O by 30-50% per query. Combined with F1 (narrow serve view), the total I/O reduction could reach 60-70%.

Impact: medium Effort: medium
Depends on: F1
Unused column removal is most effective when combined with the narrow serve view (F1), which enforces the column list at the Databricks level.
Trade-offs:
  • Must verify no external tools or ad-hoc queries depend on removed columns
  • Consider keeping columns that may be needed for future measures

F7: No aggregation tables — every query hits 6.1B-row fact at full grain

high Model-wide Engineering Semantic Model

Problem: The model has no aggregation tables. Every visual — whether showing a single KPI card or a detailed breakdown — queries the full-grain 6.1B-row fact table via DirectQuery. PBI's automatic aggregation feature could serve 80-90% of queries from a pre-aggregated Import table, falling back to DirectQuery only for drill-through to row-level detail.

How to Fix

1. Create a dbt aggregation model: agg_trade_daily_by_option_date.sql that pre-aggregates fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1 by (dim_date_sk, dim_product_option_sk, dim_pricing_store_sk) with SUM() on all metric columns. 2. Materialise as a Delta table with daily incremental refresh. 3. Add the aggregation table to the PBI model as an Import table with an Incremental Refresh policy. 4. Configure PBI aggregations: map each metric column to its DirectQuery counterpart with SUM aggregation. 5. Set the aggregation table's detail table to Daily Trade (DirectQuery). 6. Estimated aggregation table size: ~50-100M rows (vs 6.1B), refreshable in minutes.

Estimated improvement: 80-90% of queries served from Import aggregation (<1s) instead of DirectQuery (avg 2.4s, P95 9.8s). Reduces Databricks query volume by ~33K queries/day.

Impact: high Effort: high
Connection Mode Comparison:
ModeImplications
DirectQueryCurrent — every query scans 6.1B rows, avg 2.4s, P95 9.8s
Requires Deep Dive
  1. Profile which grain levels visuals actually query (page-level vs detail-level)
  2. Estimate aggregation table row count at different grain levels
  3. Test aggregation hit rate with PBI Desktop's aggregation monitoring
Trade-offs:
  • Requires creating and maintaining a new dbt model + PBI aggregation mapping
  • Aggregation table must be refreshed daily (adds to refresh pipeline)
  • Stale data between refreshes (acceptable for Trade daily snapshot)
  • Complex measures with FILTER(ALL) may not benefit from aggregations

F8: Trade report: 12 pages exceed visual density threshold (>15 visuals)

medium Report-specific Power BI

Problem: All 12 pages in the Trade report exceed the 15-visual threshold. 274 total visuals across 12 pages means an average of 23 visuals per page. Each visual in DirectQuery mode generates at least one Databricks query on page load. Pages with 20+ visuals trigger 20+ concurrent queries, competing for warehouse compute and increasing page load time.

How to Fix

1. Audit each page: identify visuals that could be moved to a drill-through page or consolidated. 2. Use bookmarks to create tabbed views that load subsets of visuals. 3. For cards showing similar metrics (e.g., 8 KPI cards), consolidate into a matrix or multi-row card. 4. Disable visual interactions where cross-filtering is not needed. 5. Target: reduce to <15 visuals per primary page.

Estimated improvement: Reducing from 23 to 15 visuals per page would cut page-load queries by ~35%, reducing concurrent Databricks query pressure.

Impact: medium Effort: medium
Trade-offs:
  • Requires report redesign and user acceptance testing
  • Drill-through pages may require additional navigation

F9: Auto-refresh enabled on Trade report

high Report-specific Power BI

Problem: The Trade report has auto-refresh enabled, which periodically re-executes all visible DirectQuery queries on a timer. With 274 visuals across 12 pages and avg query duration of 2.4s, each auto-refresh cycle generates significant Databricks load. For a daily trade snapshot that updates once per day, auto-refresh adds no value but multiplies query volume.

How to Fix

1. In Power BI Desktop, open the Trade report. 2. Go to each page's Format pane > Page refresh. 3. Disable automatic page refresh. 4. If users need a manual refresh option, add a refresh button bookmark instead.

Estimated improvement: Eliminates N x 274 unnecessary queries per auto-refresh cycle. For a 30-second refresh interval with 10 active users, this could save ~32,000 queries/hour during peak.

Impact: medium Effort: low
Trade-offs:
  • Users will need to manually refresh to see updated data
  • For a daily snapshot, manual refresh is more appropriate

F10: dim_product_option_single_valued_user_defined_attributes_v1 — slowest dimension (avg 12s, P95 40s)

high Model-wide Engineering Semantic Model

Problem: The UDA (User Defined Attributes) table averaging 12.1s per query with P95 at 40s is the slowest dimension in the model by far. Despite only 888K rows per query, the wide table (134 columns) and likely complex serve view contribute to extreme latency. With 66 queries/day, this table is a significant bottleneck when UDA-related visuals are active.

How to Fix

1. Investigate the serve view definition for dim_product_option_single_valued_user_defined_attributes_v1 — it may contain PIVOT or complex transformations causing slow execution. 2. Create a narrower serve view with only the UDA columns used in the Trade model. 3. Consider materialising this as a Delta table instead of a view if the transformation is expensive. 4. As a quick win, convert UDA from Dual to Import mode — at 888K rows, it's small enough to cache.

Estimated improvement: Converting to Import eliminates 66 12s-avg queries/day. Materialising the serve view could reduce P95 from 40s to <2s.

Impact: medium Effort: medium
Trade-offs:
  • Import mode requires scheduled refresh
  • Materialising view adds to dbt pipeline maintenance

F11: 3 pages missing date slicers — unfiltered fact table scans

medium Report-specific Power BI

Problem: 3 pages in the Trade report have data-heavy visuals but no date slicer, meaning users can trigger unfiltered queries against the 6.1B-row fact table. Without date filtering, every visual on these pages scans the full 2-year default window.

How to Fix

1. Add date slicers to the 3 identified pages. 2. Set sensible default date ranges (e.g., last 4 weeks for daily trade data). 3. Consider using report-level date filters to ensure all pages have a baseline date constraint.

Estimated improvement: Restricting to last 4 weeks (28 days out of ~730 days) could reduce scanned rows by ~96% on these pages.

Impact: medium Effort: low
Trade-offs:
  • Users may need to expand the date range for historical analysis
  • Report-level filters can be overridden by page-level slicers

F12: Engineering: 6 dbt models with functions on filter columns preventing predicate pushdown

medium Model-wide Engineering

Problem: 6 dbt models apply SQL functions (CAST, COALESCE, LOWER, etc.) on columns that are likely used in WHERE clauses or JOIN conditions. When a function wraps a column, Databricks cannot push the predicate down to the Delta file-level statistics, forcing a full file scan instead of leveraging clustering or Z-ordering.

How to Fix

1. Review each finding in engineering-bpa-results.json under rule E05. 2. Move function application to the curated layer so the serve view exposes clean columns. 3. For CAST operations, ensure data types match between tables at the curated level. 4. For COALESCE, provide default values at the curated layer.

Estimated improvement: Enables predicate pushdown on affected columns, improving clustering pruning efficiency from ~0% to 80-90% for those predicates.

Impact: medium Effort: medium
Trade-offs:
  • Requires curated-layer changes, which have wider impact across consumers

F13: 19 wide tables with >50 columns in the Trade report visual bindings

medium Report-specific Power BI

Problem: 19 visual elements in the Trade report use wide table/matrix visuals. Wide visuals bind to many columns simultaneously, each generating separate column projections in DirectQuery SQL. This amplifies the column over-selection problem described in F1.

How to Fix

1. Review each wide table/matrix visual. 2. Remove columns that are not essential for the user's analysis. 3. Use drill-through for detailed column exploration. 4. For summary pages, replace wide tables with focused KPI cards or smaller matrices.

Estimated improvement: Reducing visual column bindings by 30-50% would proportionally reduce DirectQuery column projections.

Impact: low Effort: medium
Trade-offs:
  • Users may prefer having all columns visible — discuss with stakeholders
